<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains how the ranking mechanism considers the characteristics of the goods and services offered to consumers. Bing's ranking mechanism does not generally consider the characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user (paragraph 0 and 8). However, in the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 2 and 13). Furthermore, the ranking mechanism also considers factors such as relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity (paragraph 4 and 11), as well as user engagement, location, and page load time (paragraph 6).

    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",

The output can be a response, a web result, a poem, a story, a code, an essay, a song, or anything else that can be expressed in natural language. <Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains the extent to which the ranking mechanism considers the characteristics of the goods and services offered to consumers. The characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user (paragraph 0 and 5). In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 2 and 12). However, websites cannot improve their organic ranking position by providing remuneration to Bing (paragraph 17).

    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. <Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains how the ranking mechanism considers the relevance of the characteristics of the goods and services for consumers. Bing's ranking mechanism does not directly consider the characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user (paragraph 0 and 8). However, the ranking mechanism does consider factors such as relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity (paragraph 4 and 10). Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query (paragraph 3). Quality and credibility of a website are determined by evaluating factors such as the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation (paragraph 3). User engagement, freshness of content, location, and page load time are also considered in the ranking mechanism (paragraph 3). In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 2 and 12).

<Question> Does the documentation explain the extent to which the ranking mechanism considers the relevance of the characteristics of the goods and services, for consumers?
<Answers> [
    "These features also rely on the ranking principles and main parameters described above, but in some cases take additional considerations into account to provide users with the highest quality, most relevant results available.",
    "The characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user.",
    "In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program.",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",
    "Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity.",

Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity. Bing Shopping also provides a coupons experience where coupons relevant to the user's query are displayed. <Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains that the ranking mechanism considers the relevance of the characteristics of the goods and services for consumers. Bing's complex algorithms generate search results using the user's search query, matching it with third-party webpages in their index. The relevance of the content on the landing page to the search query is a key parameter in ranking pages in search results. However, the characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user (paragraph 1, 5, 3). In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 2, 12).

<Question> Does the documentation explain how the ranking mechanism considers the design characteristics of the websites?
<Answers> [
    "For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges.",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",
    "Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity.",
    "Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content.",
    "These features also rely on the ranking principles and main parameters described above, but in some cases take additional considerations into account to provide users with the highest quality, most relevant results available.",

Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including: 1. The amount you bid for your keyword. For more information, see What are keyword bids. 2. Your ad's relevance. 3. Your ad's performance, based on various response signalsaEUR\"for example, click-through rate (CTR).",
    "Bing's image and video experiences provide the user with image and video results relevant to their search query, both on the main search results page and in the image and video verticals. Bing prioritizes relevance and may display an image or videos within search results based on query intent. Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity. Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content. Maps",
    "Ranking within conversation mode generally relies on the same parameters as the main web search results page.",

It will also help you optimize your site to increase its opportunity to rank for relevant queries in Bing's search results. Please pay special attention to the guidance in the \"Abuse section\" and examples in the \"Things to avoid\" section. Following the guidelines will ensure your site plays by the rules and is not found to be spammy, which could lead to demotion or even delisting your website from Bing search results. How Bing finds and indexes your site",

The best way to get other sites to link to your site is to create unique and high quality and unique content. Bing's crawler (Bingbot) follows links within your website (internal links) or from other sites (external links) to help Bing discover new content and new pages.",

Most SEO practices render a website more appealing to Bing; however, performing SEO-related work does not guarantee rankings will improve or sites will receive an increase in traffic from Bing. Further, taken to extremes, some SEO practices can be abused, resulting in penalties by search engines. These Bing Webmaster Guidelines describe only some of the most widespread forms of inappropriate, manipulative, or misleading behaviors. Sites that engage in abuse, such as the practices outlined below, are considered low quality. As a result, these sites can incur ranking penalties, have site markup ignored, and may not be selected for indexing. Microsoft may take action against your site for any inappropriate or deceptive practices, even those not described here. If you feel action is taken against your site, you can contact our support team through the Bing Webmaster Tools. By creating clear, unique, high-quality, relevant, and easy-to-find content on your website, you will increase the probability of Bing indexing and showing your content in search results. Content: Websites that are thin on content, show ads or affiliate links primarily, or redirect visitors away to other sites quickly tend to drop in rankings on Bing. In some cases, it may not get indexed at all. Your content should be easy to navigate, rich and engaging to the website visitor, and provide the information they seek."

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains how the ranking mechanism considers the design characteristics of the websites. Bing's ranking mechanism considers factors such as relevance, quality and credibility, user engagement, freshness, location, and page load time. The quality and credibility of a website are evaluated based on the clarity of the site's purpose, its usability, presentation, authoritativeness, and the completeness of the content. Bing also considers how users interact with search results, including whether users click through to search results for a given query, spend time on these search results, or adjust or reformulate their query. The freshness of the content and the page load time are also considered in the ranking mechanism. Bing prefers fresh content and views slow page load times as a poor user experience (paragraph 1).

<Question> Does the documentation explain the extent to which the ranking mechanism considers the design characteristics of the websites?
<Answers> [
    "Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity.",
    "For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges.",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",
    "These features also rely on the ranking principles and main parameters described above, but in some cases take additional considerations into account to provide users with the highest quality, most relevant results available.",
    "Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content.",

Most SEO practices render a website more appealing to Bing; however, performing SEO-related work does not guarantee rankings will improve or sites will receive an increase in traffic from Bing. Further, taken to extremes, some SEO practices can be abused, resulting in penalties by search engines. These Bing Webmaster Guidelines describe only some of the most widespread forms of inappropriate, manipulative, or misleading behaviors. Sites that engage in abuse, such as the practices outlined below, are considered low quality. As a result, these sites can incur ranking penalties, have site markup ignored, and may not be selected for indexing. If you feel action is taken against your site, you can contact our support team through the Bing Webmaster Tools. Additionally, users can report abuse of any of these practices using the feedback link in the footer of bing.com after performing a search that reproduces the issue. Bing prioritizes relevance and may display an image or videos within search results based on query intent. Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity. Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content. Maps",

Following the guidelines will ensure your site plays by the rules and is not found to be spammy, which could lead to demotion or even delisting your website from Bing search results. How Bing finds and indexes your site",

Bing's crawler (Bingbot) follows links within your website (internal links) or from other sites (external links) to help Bing discover new content and new pages.",

Content: Websites that are thin on content, show ads or affiliate links primarily, or redirect visitors away to other sites quickly tend to drop in rankings on Bing. In some cases, it may not get indexed at all. Your content should be easy to navigate, rich and engaging to the website visitor, and provide the information they seek."

Creating cache <./cache/cache_exp4_bing/qa_embedder-edu_amr_clause.pkl>..
<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains the extent to which the ranking mechanism considers the design characteristics of the websites. Bing's ranking mechanism considers the relevance of the content on the landing page to the search query, including matching terms and semantic equivalents (paragraph 2). The quality and credibility of a website are evaluated based on factors such as the clarity of the site's purpose, its usability, presentation, authoritativeness, and the completeness of the content (paragraph 2). User engagement is also considered, including how users interact with search results and their behavior on the webpages (paragraph 2). Other factors include the freshness of the content, the user's location, the page load time, and the location of other visitors to the page (paragraph 2). The characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user (paragraph 6). Websites that are thin on content, show ads or affiliate links primarily, or redirect visitors away to other sites quickly tend to drop in rankings on Bing (paragraph 18).

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains the possibilities to influence ranking against direct or indirect payment. In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 0 and 4). However, Bing does not allow websites to improve their organic ranking positions through payment (paragraph 1 and 2). Websites may choose to advertise on Bing through Microsoft Advertising, but they cannot improve their organic ranking position by providing remuneration to Bing (paragraph 2). Ad position, which is where ads appear on Bing, AOL, Yahoo, or a partner site's search engine results page, is determined by how it ranks against competing ads. Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including the amount you bid for your keyword, your ad's relevance, and your ad's performance (paragraph 8).

<Question> Does the documentation explain how the ranking mechanism works and, in particular, what the main parameters used are?
<Answers> [
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains how the ranking mechanism works and the main parameters used. The ranking mechanism is based on complex algorithms that use machine learning to identify patterns in data and generalize based on a small set of examples. The main parameters used to rank pages in search results, listed in general order of importance, are: 

1. Relevance: This refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning (paragraph 0).

2. Quality and Credibility: This includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. It also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse, the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship (paragraph 0).

3. User engagement: Bing considers how users interact with search results. This includes whether users click through to search results for a given query, which results they click on, whether they spend time on these search results or quickly return to Bing, and whether the user adjusts or reformulates their query (paragraph 0).

4. Freshness: Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh (paragraph 0).

5. Location: Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page (paragraph 0).

6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result (paragraph 0). 

For ad ranking, the position is determined by multiple factors, including the amount you bid for your keyword, your ad's relevance, and your ad's performance, based on various response signals, for example, click-through rate (CTR) (paragraph 1).

Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including: 1. The amount you bid for your keyword. For more information, see What are keyword bids. 2. Your ad's relevance. 3.     "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",

Bing Maps relies on licensed and publicly available location data and uses the same ranking parameters mentioned above. Businesses can participate in the Bing Maps experience and manage their listing by registering with Bing Places. News",
    "Bing seeks rich, valuable, and engaging content created for users, not search engines. By creating clear, unique, high-quality, relevant, and easy-to-find content on your website, you will increase the probability of Bing indexing and showing your content in search results. Content: Websites that are thin on content, show ads or affiliate links primarily, or redirect visitors away to other sites quickly tend to drop in rankings on Bing. In some cases, it may not get indexed at all. Your content should be easy to navigate, rich and engaging to the website visitor, and provide the information they seek."

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains what is most important in determining ranking. The main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results are listed in general order of importance: Relevance, Quality and Credibility, User engagement, Freshness, Location, and Page load time. Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. Quality and Credibility of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. User engagement considers how users interact with search results. Freshness refers to how up-to-date the information is. Location takes into account the user's location, where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. Page load time is also important as slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere (paragraph 3). 

Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including: The amount you bid for your keyword, your ad's relevance, and your ad's performance, based on various response signalsfor example, click-through rate (CTR) (paragraph 2). 

Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity. Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content (paragraph 10).

<Question> Does the documentation explain why specific parameters were selected as the main factors in determining the ranking of goods or services?
<Answers> [
    "These features also rely on the ranking principles and main parameters described above, but in some cases take additional considerations into account to provide users with the highest quality, most relevant results available.",
    "These parameters are listed in general order of importance.",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",
    "The characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user.",
    "Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity.",
    "Ad position is where your ads appear on Bing, AOL, Yahoo, or a partner site's search engine results page. Your ad's position is determined by how it ranks against competing ads. Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including: 1. The amount you bid for your keyword. For more information, see What are keyword bids. 2. Your ad's relevance. 3. Your ad's performance, based on various response signalsaEUR\"for example, click-through rate (CTR).",
    "In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program.",
    "In the Bing Maps experience, users can type queries into the search bar, and the map will display a list of locations in that vicinity responsive to that search or pinpoint a particular address. Bing Maps relies on licensed and publicly available location data and uses the same ranking parameters mentioned above. Businesses can participate in the Bing Maps experience and manage their listing by registering with Bing Places. News",
    "For example, if you sell shoes and bid on the keyword \"shoe,\" you'll have to beat the ad rank of the other advertisers who are also bidding on \"shoe.\"",
    "The characteristics of the goods or services offered on a site do not affect how Bing ranks results, except in cases where the content is potentially offensive or harmful to a user. For example, pages offering adult content are not available when users set SafeSearch to \"Strict\" mode. As another example, pages promoting potentially harmful content, such as where a site promotes methods of suicide or purports to sell opioids or other potentially harmful drugs, may be downranked as low authority.",

    "Bing's image and video experiences provide the user with image and video results relevant to their search query, both on the main search results page and in the image and video verticals. Bing prioritizes relevance and may display an image or videos within search results based on query intent. Ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity. Ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content. Maps",

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains why specific parameters were selected as the main factors in determining the ranking of goods or services. The main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results are relevance, quality and credibility, user engagement, freshness, location, and page load time. Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. Quality and credibility of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. User engagement considers how users interact with search results. Freshness refers to how up-to-date the information on the page is. Location takes into account the user's location, where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. Page load time is important as slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave a website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result (paragraph 2).

<Answers> [
    "These features also rely on the ranking principles and main parameters described above, but in some cases take additional considerations into account to provide users with the highest quality, most relevant results available.",
    "For example, if you sell shoes and bid on the keyword \"shoe,\" you'll have to beat the ad rank of the other advertisers who are also bidding on \"shoe.\"",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains the internal process conducted by the provider to determine the main parameters for the ranking of goods or services. The main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results are relevance, quality and credibility, user engagement, freshness, location, and page load time. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing uses complex algorithms and machine learning to identify patterns in data and generalize based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals (paragraph 2). The ranking inputs are derived from the content meta-data and a deep learning algorithmic review of the content (paragraph 4). The ranking within the image and video experiences generally rely on the same parameters as the main web search results page, i.e., relevance, quality, freshness, authority, and popularity (paragraph 5). Ad rank is determined by multiple factors, including the amount you bid for your keyword, your ad's relevance, and your ad's performance, based on various response signalsfor example, click-through rate (CTR) (paragraph 7). In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 8).

    "For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges.",
    "Complex algorithms generate Microsoft Bing search results using the user's search query matching it with third-party webpages in our index. Bing designs and continually improves its algorithms to provide the most comprehensive, relevant, and valuable collection of search results available. Given the scale of the internet and the complexity of operating a search engine, Bing relies on machine learning to ensure users see the best results for their query out of the trillions of pages of content on the web. Machine learning is the science of getting computers to act without being explicitly programmed by identifying patterns in data and generalizing based on a small set of examples. For web ranking, this means building a model that will look at some ideal results to learn which features are most predictive of their usefulness, relying on automated signals like user interactions with the Bing website and training data labeled by human judges. Bing guides its judges to make sure their evaluations align with Bing's ranking goals. Below is a high-level overview of the main parameters Bing uses to rank pages in search results. These parameters are listed in general order of importance. Bing's complex systems use these criteria to deliver search results, and the relative importance of each of the parameters below may vary from search to search and evolve overtime: 1. Relevance: Relevance refers to how closely the content on the landing page matches the intent behind the search query. This includes matching terms directly on the page and phrases used in links referring to the page. Bing also considers semantic equivalents, including synonyms or abbreviations, which may not be exact matches of the query terms but are understood to have the same meaning. Many queries may have more than one possible intent. Bing tries to provide a comprehensive set of results that reflect all possible intents. Bing presumes the user seeks high-quality, authoritative content unless the user clearly indicates an intent to find low-authority content. 2. Quality and Credibility: Determining the quality and credibility (QC) of a website includes evaluating the clarity of purpose of the site, its usability, and presentation. QC also consists of an evaluation of the page's authoritativeness, which includes such factors as the author's or site's reputation, the level of discourse (for example, an article with citations and references to data sources is considered higher quality than one that does not explain or cite it's data sources; pages that call for violence, name-calling, offensive statements, or use derogatory language to make a point are generally considered low quality), the completeness of the content, and transparency of authorship 3. User engagement: Bing also considers how users interact with search results. To determine user engagement, Bing asks questions like: Did users click through to search results for a given query, and if so, which results? Did users spend time on these search results they clicked through or quickly return to Bing? Did the user adjust or reformulate their query? The Bing Webmaster Dashboard will provide insights into how users interact with your webpages. 4. Freshness: Generally, Bing prefers fresh content. The page that consistently provides up-to-date information is considered fresh. In many cases, content produced today will still be relevant years from now. In some cases, however, content produced today will go out of date quickly. 5. Location: In ranking results, Bing considers the user's location (country and city), where the page is hosted, the language of the page, and the location of other visitors to the page. 6. Page load time: Slow page load times can lead a visitor to leave your website, potentially before the content has even loaded, to seek information elsewhere. Bing may view this as a poor user experience and a less helpful search result. Faster page loads are always better, but webmasters should balance absolute page load speed with a positive, useful user experience.",

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation does explain how users can improve the ranking of their goods or services. Users can improve their ad rank and position by following suggestions provided by Bing (paragraph 3). They can also stand out by sharing images, product ratings, and promotions of the products they're selling (paragraph 4, 8). In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 7, 11). Users can also optimize their keyword bids to improve performance and increase their ROI (paragraph 12, 18). Furthermore, creating clear, unique, high-quality, relevant, and easy-to-find content on the website can increase the probability of Bing indexing and showing the content in search results (paragraph 6).

The reality is that social media schemes are easy to see in action, and the website's value is deprecated. One such example is auto follow. Auto follows encourage follower growth on social sites such as Twitter, and work by automatically following anyone who follows you. Over time this creates a scenario where the number of followers you have is more or less the same as the number of people following you. This does not indicate you have a strong influence. Following few people while having a high follower count would indicate a stronger influential voice."

<Final Answer> Yes, the documentation explains how users can alter the ranking of their products or services through direct or indirect payments to the provider. In the Bing Shopping experience, the ranking may be influenced by payment from sellers participating in the Microsoft Shopping program (paragraph 0 and 1). However, websites cannot improve their organic ranking position by providing remuneration to Bing (paragraph 2 and 3). The documentation also explains that the ad position, which can affect the visibility of products or services, is determined by multiple factors including the amount bid for a keyword (paragraph 18).
